British Chancellor of the Exchequer Reports on Military and Diplomatic Situation in the House of Commons, Calls Dutch and Belgian Peace Appeals a Courageous Act, Alliance Between Britain and France Grows Stronger

London: Chancellor of the Exchequer Simon, representing Prime Minister Chamberlain, delivered a speech in the House of Commons today, reporting on the diplomatic and military situation of the past week. He first mentioned the peace appeals issued by the heads of state of Belgium and the Netherlands, calling them courageous acts. However, he also said that Chamberlain had previously stated that, based on past experience, it was difficult to expect the German government to submit a satisfactory reply. King George VI of Britain had declared in a reply to the heads of state of Belgium and the Netherlands that any proposal that could form a reasonable basis for peace would be considered. However, German head of state Hitler gave a speech in Munich on the 9th of this month, deliberately misinterpreting British policy. The country's propaganda machine then distorted the replies submitted by Britain and France, claiming that they rejected the peace appeals. This shows that the answer submitted by the country did not open the door to a satisfactory peace solution. According to German official announcements, Foreign Minister Ribbentrop notified the envoys of Belgium and the Netherlands yesterday in the name of Hitler, saying that since the peace proposal had been rejected by Britain and France, the German government had no choice but to consider it hopeless. This is also a sophistry. As for the military situation of the past week, rumors of German aggression against Belgium and the Netherlands are rampant. The British government, in accordance with its consistent policy, is very willing to respect the neutrality of these countries. However, given the large number of German troops concentrated in areas bordering Belgium and the Netherlands, and the open threats made by the country's newspapers against these countries, German aggression is imminent. All discerning people have already seen through this. Under such circumstances, it is to be expected that countries around the world unanimously despise Germany's superficially expressed peaceful words. No one in our country overestimates these words, and it is unnecessary to repeat them. As for the naval war, many enemy merchant ships are still docked in their own or neutral ports, and dare not sail as usual. In the past week, a total of four enemy ships were intercepted by our side. On the 12th and 13th of this month, enemy ships were scuttled by their crews. As for the air war, enemy planes once raided the Shetland Islands in our country. In addition, the air forces of both sides have been very active in recent days, mostly in fragmented actions, and no fierce battles have occurred. In general, there has been no special activity in the military field in the past half month, but the strength of our country's military and the determination of our nation have been fully demonstrated." As for the international situation in the past half month, the position of the allied countries of Britain and France has become stronger and stronger. "After the establishment of the new U.S. Neutrality Act, it has been able to continue to supply us with the armaments that it can supply. This is very important. As for the negotiations between Finland and the Soviet Union, they have in fact broken down, which is disappointing." In addition, Polish Prime Minister Sikorski is currently holding talks with our authorities here to discuss the issue of the country's army joining the Allied forces. As for the visit of French Finance Minister Reynaud, the two sides discussed various economic and financial issues, proving that their views are completely consistent. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

British Cruiser Captures German Ship

London: A British cruiser recently captured a German ship at sea yesterday and ordered it to sail to a port in the west. All two or three dozen crew members have landed. This ship is probably the "Leonté" (900 tons). At the beginning of the European war, it had taken refuge in the Spanish port of Vigo and only attempted to escape its internment now. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

London: The Ministry of Economic Warfare announced that the British Contraband Control Committee detained 6,500 tons of contraband suspected of being shipped to Germany in the week ending November 11. During the same week, the committee considered 108 ship cases, and 86 cases that had not been resolved in the previous week. Two batches of goods were completely confiscated, 88 were completely released, and 43 had some goods confiscated. On November 11, there were 94 neutral ships berthed at the base of the British Contraband Control, 58 of which had been berthed at the base for less than a week. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

The Hague: According to a statement from the British Wartime Economic Bureau, 108 ships arrived at the southern seaports of Britain from November 5 to 11 to await inspection. The week before that, 86 ships arrived to await inspection, and they are still under British control and have not regained their freedom. It is reported that after inspection, the cargo of two ships was completely confiscated, and the cargo of 43 ships was partially confiscated. The cargo of 88 ships has already been released. However, according to a survey on November 14, there are still 94 neutral ships docked in British-controlled seaports. (Haitong dispatch, 16th)

Encounters on Various Parts of the Western Front

Paris: The General Headquarters issued War Bulletin No. 146, stating, "Patrols from both sides engaged in encounters on various parts of the front today, and artillery fire from both sides was also very active." (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Paris: The General Headquarters issued War Bulletin No. 147, stating, "Nothing worthy of mention occurred on the front last night." (Havas dispatch, 16th)

Paris: Le Petit Parisien today published an article by Maurice, saying that both sides on the Western Front now seem to be waiting for the right moment to act, and the reported fighting is only a matter of some activity by the pickets. German pickets are only composed of a small number of soldiers in the dense forest areas of the Moselle and Rhine positions, located in the northeast area of Bitche and between the Lauter River, which has been the destination of German activity in the past few days. The Germans have also sent many reconnaissance patrols to operate in the lower reaches of the Vosges River to investigate the location of French resistance. The French are also engaged in reconnaissance, in enemy concentration areas outside the French line of defence, according to today's Figaro. German artillery recently engaged in firing at a certain point in the Moselle River area, (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Several Ships Continue to Sink in European Waters, Two Lithuanian Ships and Two British Ships

Lithuanian National Capital: The Lithuanian cargo ships "Panaman" (2,400 tons) and "Nidan" (1,900 tons) recently sank one after another in the Estonian sea in the Baltic Sea. The "Nidan" was carrying a batch of British coal. The fate of the crew of the two ships is still unknown. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

London: The British oil tanker Woodtown (794 tons) sank within one minute after an explosion today. Nine crew members drowned and four were sent to the hospital. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

London: The British ship "George" (2,316 tons) recently struck a derelict ship floating in the northeastern waters of Britain and sank as a result. All crew members have been rescued. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Panama: The British regular liner "Matararo" (12,390 tons) recently arrived here. According to the crew, the ship was chased by a German submarine for 50 minutes en route from Britain to New Zealand. The British ship was eventually spared because of its greater speed. When the German submarine was first sighted, it was two and a half miles away. The captain immediately turned the wheel and accelerated forward. The submarine chased behind until it was about seven miles away. Although the British ship had defensive equipment, the captain said that he was ordered not to open fire unless attacked. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Beijing: The Belgian small steamer "Maurice, Margaret" sank in Dunkirk after hitting a French mine. Three sailors were buried at sea. (Haitong dispatch, 16th)

Britain Trains Air Force Across the Country

London: It is reported that two young air force officers who recently won the British Empire Medal previously learned aviation as bus drivers and members of a flying club, practicing for half an hour a day. After half a month, they obtained a pilot's license. In April of this year, they were promoted to junior officers in the Air Force, and now they have won the officer's Empire Medal for their proficiency in skills and courageous behavior. This shows the effectiveness of British pilot training. This training system has now been implemented in all parts of the Empire. The main training center is currently in Canada, with 4,000 people currently being trained and 10,000 to 15,000 people on the waiting list. India has now opened an Indian Air Force training station, and local princes are donating huge sums of money to develop air defenses, and the Prince of Hyderabad is even paying for the entire team of an air force detachment. Because there is gasoline supply in Iraq, it is also engaged in pilot training. Trainees from Australia will be trained in Egypt because the climate in Egypt is especially suitable. As for Germany, due to limited oil reserves, pilot training is very difficult, which is very different from the convenience of Britain. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Rumor of Britain and France Forming a Customs Union Denied by British Officials

London: There were rumours spreading that after French Finance Minister Reynaud came here and held talks with Finance Minister Simon, the two countries could form a customs union. However, official sources recently emphatically denied this, saying, "The talks were limited to technical issues arising from economic cooperation. For example, issues such as currency and exchange controls, and promoting trade, were all submitted for discussion, but both sides have no intention of unifying currencies at present, and France has never proposed this. In general, Britain and France have completely consistent views on current issues, but there is no need to establish a customs union" (Havas dispatch, 16th)

German Planes Attack Shetland, Bombs Miss

London: According to the latest news, when German planes raided the Shetland Islands twice on Sunday, at least 16 heavy bombs were dropped. The previous report of 12 was inaccurate. Four of the bombs were deeply embedded in a certain muddy mountain area and did not explode. They were found last night and were all bombs capable of penetrating armor, each weighing about 250 pounds. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

German-Swedish Business Negotiations

Berlin: A spokesman for the German Foreign Ministry yesterday denied the report that Germany had put forward certain demands during business negotiations with Sweden. The spokesman said that the German-Swedish business negotiations are temporarily suspended, and the representatives of the two sides are waiting for new instructions from the government. (Haitong dispatch, 16th)

Germany Intensifies Training of Officers

Paris: According to reliable sources here, there is evidence to indicate that Germany is actively striving to train officers through mass production methods. It is reported that Germany is still short of 15,000 officers, and even among the front-line officers, many lack sufficient experience. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Soviet-German Consultations on Opening Air Route

Moscow: More than 40 people from German business circles arrived here yesterday, including four representatives from German airlines, who will consult with the Soviet authorities on opening an air route between Moscow and Berlin (via Warsaw). In addition, there are many Germans, most of whom are also from business circles, now in Leningrad. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Hungary Cracks Down on Political Activities

Hungarian National Capital: Interior Minister Fecher delivered a speech in the House of Representatives yesterday evening, stating, "The government will do its utmost to suppress any kind of incitement." Members of the Parliament here were very satisfied after hearing this, saying, "The authorities of this country arrested several members of the National Socialist Party a few weeks ago. The party's members immediately withdrew from the House of Representatives to protest. Now, Interior Minister Fecher has made this speech in response to the party, which is deeply supported by the majority of members of other parties in the Parliament," (Havas dispatch, 16th)

British Trade Delegation Arrives in Madrid

Madrid: A British trade delegation has now arrived here and will begin negotiations with the Spanish authorities in order to amend existing trade agreements between Britain and Spain in accordance with wartime conditions. (Reuters dispatch, 16th)

Japanese Ambassador to Italy, Amau, Arrives

Rome: The Japanese Ambassador to Italy, Amau (formerly Minister to Switzerland), arrived here this afternoon to take office. Representatives from the Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs and staff from the Japanese Embassy welcomed him at the station. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

US Newspapers Advocate Maintaining an Independent Policy in the Far East, Cautioning Against British and French Flattery of Japan

New York: The New York Daily News today warned the United States to be wary of the Allies' "flattery of Japan." It said, "We must remember that Britain and France never supported the United States in taking a firm stance against Japan's conquest of Manchuria in 1931." The newspaper's editorial was titled "Flattery of Japan," and solemnly stated the importance of the United States maintaining an independent policy in the Far East, saying that after Britain and France withdraw their troops stationed in China, there is no reason for the United States' Far East policy to soften. "If we abandon our independent policy, we will gain nothing and will suffer all kinds of losses. It is very clear that the Allies are bargaining with Japan. A replay of the events of 1931 is happening. In 1931, we alone strongly protested against the Japanese military's invasion of Manchuria, while Britain isolated the United States and did not support it" (United Press dispatch, 16th)

Washington: The Standard Star newspaper recently commented on the withdrawal of some troops stationed in North China by Britain and France, briefly stating that Britain and France have not abandoned their rights in China, and the firm attitude taken by the United States government should be maintained. "The U.S. government is about to announce the abrogation of the 1911 U.S.-Japan trade agreement, and is also consolidating naval bases in the Pacific. In addition, the U.S. Ambassador to Japan recently expressed his dissatisfaction with the Japanese military's actions in China during a speech in Tokyo. The U.S. government has also sent a submarine fleet to the East Asian seas. All of this, in Japan's view, should be regarded as a warning that although the war hawks in that country want to exclude third countries in the Far East, the Western countries will not be willing to back down" (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Cornerstone Laid for Statue of Former US President Jefferson, Roosevelt Attends and Speaks

Washington: The city is building a statue of the late President Jefferson, and the cornerstone laying ceremony was held yesterday. President Roosevelt personally attended and delivered a speech. "I very much hope to come again to participate in the unveiling ceremony of the late President's statue in January 1941." People then commented that President Roosevelt's term of office was originally due to expire on March 4, 1941, and what he said may imply that he will still submit his candidacy in next year's election, which is not impossible. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

Tonnage of New US Cruisers May Increase

Washington: Acting Secretary of the Navy Edison recently gave a speech to the press, saying that the US Navy has obtained extremely valuable lessons from observing the ongoing war in Europe, which can be used to build the new cruisers "Columbia" and "Crane Fulun." According to the current shipbuilding program, the tonnage of these two ships is 8,000 tons, and construction has not yet begun. However, since the provision in the London Naval Treaty prohibiting the construction of 10,000-ton cruisers has lost its effect due to Japan's lack of restraint, the tonnage of the "Columbia" and "Crane Fulun" may be increased. Regarding this level, well-informed sources here say that these new cruisers may be modeled after the German pocket cruisers. However, Secretary Edison said that the German pocket cruisers have not proven to be superior to similar warships from other countries, and the United States can still build better cruisers. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

New Antarctic Land to Belong to the United States

Boston: The first Antarctic expedition to be organized by the US government in a century has decided that the motor ship North Star, which is setting out for the first time, will set sail for Little America near Antarctica today. The leader of the expedition, the famous explorer Admiral Byrd, will board the North Star later and declare that the land he has discovered belongs to the United States. He believes that it can be a safer new base for aviation between the United States and Australia. According to reports, Byrd was the first person to fly over the North and South Poles and one of the first to fly across the Atlantic. He completed these three great achievements in three and a half years, so he became famous before he turned forty. Byrd also made a name for himself in the US Naval Aviation Corps during the war. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Rosemary Wins Lawsuit

London. Judge Burke of the High Court ruled today on Princess Hohenlohe's case against Lord Rosemary for breach of contract, finding in favor of Lord Rosemary. All allegations were dismissed. The plaintiff made two claims: (1) Damages for wrongful dismissal or cancellation of the employment contract. The court found that there was no stipulation preventing the plaintiff from accepting 25,000 pounds from an American publisher for publishing Hungarian sports manuscripts. Furthermore, the plaintiff's salary was paid until the end of 1938, at which point the contract would have expired without any notice from either party. (2) The defendant's obligation, in January 1933, to clear the plaintiff's name regarding defamatory news published in a French newspaper and to provide financial assistance. The court found that the defendant never assumed an obligation in the contract to clear the plaintiff's name or agreed in the contract to provide an annual allowance of 5,000 pounds to support the plaintiff for life. As for the confidential documents presented in court, none of them contained anything that would damage the reputation of the defendant or the sender. Any person of repute would naturally not want confidential correspondence with foreign heads of state to be disclosed in court. The court also found that the plaintiff obtained copies of these letters not from her employer, the defendant, but from individuals in Europe who corresponded with the defendant. The plaintiff has not provided a satisfactory explanation for how this occurred. Moreover, the plaintiff has been unable to continue obtaining confidential letters from the German Chancellery since January 1929, that the defendant had sent to the German Chancellery. (Reuters, 15th)

Soviet Furs Shipped to Germany

Berlin. The Leipzig Fur Trade Delegation recently returned from Leningrad, where they inspected Soviet furs. It is reported that the Soviet Union will ship furs worth one million marks to Germany, including 14,000 Persian lambskins and 400 silver fox pelts. (Haitong Telegraph, 16th)

Soviet-Finnish Relations Worsen; Finland Actively Prepares; Finnish Representative Claims Negotiations Still Sought

Helsinki. After the Finnish delegation returned here from Moscow, the Finnish cabinet convened a cabinet meeting to discuss whether the Finnish government should make a final effort to promote the resumption of Soviet-Finnish negotiations through diplomatic channels. It is also learned that the Soviet Minister to Finland is currently in Moscow and is not expected to return to his post for the time being. (Reuters, 16th)

Swiss National Capital. A correspondent for the Neue Zürcher Zeitung in the Finnish National Capital recently wired that, according to Finnish military sources, regardless of the outcome of future talks between Finland and the Soviet Union, the Finnish National Government will maintain all precautionary measures taken until the end of the European war. However, the current troop levels will be reduced as the defensive works currently under construction are completed. It is also reported that responsible individuals in the country stated that the Finnish National economic and financial situation is very sound, preparations have not yet been utilized, and it will not be difficult to maintain the current precautionary measures to the greatest extent possible. Considering that Finland's foreign debt, calculated per capita, requires only one thousand Finnish marks per person, one can see the extremely good financial situation. (Havas, 16th)

Moscow. Soviet newspapers have recently been attacking Finnish reactionaries, claiming that they want to extend their country's borders to the Soviet Ural Mountains. At the same time, they are fiercely conducting anti-Soviet propaganda, falsely claiming that Soviet Russia is the same as Tsarist Russia, and failing to recognize that their country's independence was restored thanks to the Soviet October Revolution. Finnish newspapers have been inciting hatred towards the Soviet Union, and the Finnish authorities have even been guiding the people by killing Soviet soldiers. In short, the country is now leaning towards Western countries, especially those that have always been hostile to the Soviet Union. (Havas, 16th)

Helsinki. After meeting with the President, the chief representative of the Finnish delegation, Paasikivi, met with journalists yesterday and stated that neither Finland nor the Soviet Union has explicitly stated that the Soviet-Finnish negotiations have broken down, but the date for resuming negotiations has not yet been decided. Finland is still prepared to continue negotiations with the Soviet Union. At the same time, Finland fully trusts the treaties previously signed with the Soviet Union. Regarding the state of military preparations in Finland, Paasikivi declined to comment. Paasikivi then solemnly denied that Soviet aircraft had attacked Finnish coastal cities. (Haitong Telegraph, 16th)

Helsinki. The Moscow radio station today again attacked Finland with strong words, accusing the Finnish rulers of being under the protection of Britain. This is the second attack on Finland by the Moscow radio station since the suspension of Soviet-Finnish negotiations. The first attack occurred on the day the Finnish delegation was recalled, accusing Finland of failing to notify the Soviet authorities of the flood threat from border rivers. This second attack occurred shortly after the Finnish representative arrived in Finland. The chief Finnish representative, Paasikivi, told people after returning home that the Soviet claim of Finnish economic difficulties was absurd and that economic pressure from the Soviet side had no effect on Finland. Finland is currently implementing various precautionary plans to cope with other possible difficulties. (Reuters, 15th)

Danzig. According to the Danzig Times today, citing as-yet-unconfirmed reports, the Soviet Union is planning to abolish the Soviet-Finnish Non-Aggression Treaty. Finnish sources also claim that Finland has completed the construction of fortresses and defensive works in the area bordering the Soviet Union, and Finnish troops have moved into new positions to defend them. As for the neuro-warfare that the Soviet Union intends to adopt, Finland is also prepared to experience it. It is expected here that after the Finnish Finance Minister Tanner returns here from Moscow, he will issue several laws restricting the economy and finances to cope with the pressure from the Soviet side. At the same time, Finnish officials are confident that Finland will be able to borrow foreign debt, at least from Sweden and the United States. Domestically, the government's national defense bonds worth ten million US dollars have been fully sold, and the Finnish people's patriotic donations have reached as much as 1.5 million US dollars. (United Press, 16th)

Helsinki. A large storm occurred in the Gulf of Finland, and the water level of the Neva River rose three feet, causing considerable damage to the village of Leningrad. The Soviet side therefore criticized Finland, claiming that if Finland's weather reports had not stopped, the residents of Leningrad would have been able to take precautions. However, according to Finnish newspapers, Finland's weather reports have been stopped for several months, not just today, but have only recently been resumed. Therefore, the Soviet side's criticism is completely unfounded. Furthermore, according to reports from Tallinn, Estonia, a large storm occurred in the Gulf of Finland, damaging many of the Soviet seaplanes parked there. (United Press, 16th)

Moscow. Professor Bakh, a well-known Soviet biologist and member of the Academy of Sciences, (who attended the Supreme Soviet as a representative,) published an article in the Soviet trade union newspaper today, expressing indignation at the United States' interference in the Soviet Union's negotiations with Finland, and warning the United States to "mind its own business and not interfere in the affairs of others." According to Professor Bakh, President Roosevelt's sudden expression of concern for Finland has surprised the Soviet public, because the threat to Finland is not the Soviet Union, but its domestic leaders. The Finnish reactionaries are now acting as tools for war provocateurs, placing Finland entirely on a war footing, and causing the lives of the Finnish people to decline day by day. Moreover, the demands made by the Soviet Union on Finland are not only extremely reasonable, but have been conceded as much as possible. Our demands are absolutely indispensable to the Soviet Union. I firmly believe that the Soviet government will be able to carry out its original intentions to defend our industrial capital. Anyone who interferes with this action of the Soviet Union must be repelled with extreme determination. The United States, as a country of gold and monetary imperialism, has placed the entire Americas under its control in the name of the Monroe Doctrine. What qualifications does it have to speak on the actions of the Soviet Union? (United Press, 16th)

Italy Maintains Armed Peace; Mussolini's Speech

Rome. Premier Mussolini delivered a speech yesterday from the balcony of the Palazzo Venezia to tens of thousands of people, including several thousand students. He said, "You must study in calmness and discipline, and keep a gun by your books. What our country wants to maintain is armed peace, not cowardly peace." Informed sources here commented that this is further proof that Italy is still taking a wait-and-see attitude towards the current European war. However, Italy is ready and will assume a peace mission when the opportunity arises. The entire meaning of the Prime Minister's speech regarding all current events is nothing more than that. Some observers also said that during yesterday's demonstration, the students shouted slogans such as "Corsica Tunis," but the crowd did not respond. However, Italy's desire for the Mediterranean and North African French territories has not been abandoned and can still be seen here. (Havas, 15th)

Rome. Italian Daily editor Gaida broadcasted to the United States today, saying that Italy hopes for a solution to the colonial problem. Italy was sold out by the Treaty of Versailles, which did not give Italy colonies. Italy's goal is the political and economic harmony of the Balkan countries and the free and equal solution of the colonial problem. Prime Minister Mussolini's calm and armed policy is based on waiting and vigilance. (Reuters, 16th)

New British Ambassador to France Presents Credentials; Anglo-French Sincere Cooperation

Paris. The new British Ambassador, Sir Campbell, went to the Presidential Palace this morning to present his credentials to President Lebrun, and delivered a eulogy, stating that both countries can cooperate sincerely, fully understand each other, and must work together to cope with the current dangers. He said, "When my predecessor, Sir Phipps, presented his credentials to Your Excellency several years ago, our two countries already had the desire to maintain peace, and later made many efforts, but the desire for peace ultimately became a bubble. Today, our two nations are forced to fight against aggressive countries in order to defend a tradition of hundreds of years, and are well aware that the safety of the territory and the future are shaken. Only by achieving victory can we enjoy peaceful happiness and protect the right to exist. To achieve victory, our two countries must be united. As far as my country is concerned, we deeply admire the bravery and calmness of the people of your country, and will cooperate with all national resources. The fate of Europe depends on how our two countries cooperate. I am very honored to be able to contribute to this." President Lebrun immediately replied, "Your two countries' thoughts and actions are absolutely consistent, and the close relationship between the two countries is unprecedented." (Havas, 16th)

Dutch-Belgian Peace Proposal; Germany Responds; Believes This Movement Has Ended; German Foreign Minister Meets with Belgian and Dutch Envoys

Swiss National Capital. According to Berlin sources, German Foreign Minister Ribbentrop met with Belgian Ambassador Davignon and Dutch Minister Weede this morning and informed them in the name of Führer Hitler that the German government had no choice but to consider the peace proposal of Belgium and the Netherlands to have failed since it had been rejected by Britain and France. (Havas, 15th)

Paris. Diplomatic figures here commented on the fact that the German government did not respond to the peace proposal by the heads of Belgium and the Netherlands until today, saying that this is further proof that Germany's strategy is to shift the responsibility for prolonging the war onto Britain and France. Earlier, Belgium and the Netherlands had come forward to mediate once in late August, at which time Germany rejected it, claiming that it was launched too late and that the move was sufficient to facilitate Britain and France. Now it is openly said that the peace that the heads of Belgium and the Netherlands decided to mediate could not be realized because of the answers from Britain and France, hoping to deceive world opinion. It only sees its efforts being unsuccessful. (Havas, 15th)

Belgian Capital Brussels. After German Foreign Minister Ribbentrop rejected the peace proposal of the heads of Belgium and the Netherlands in the name of Führer Hitler, well-informed sources here declared that the German government may not issue a formal note again, but Führer Hitler may send a telegram to the heads of Belgium and the Netherlands in a private capacity to explain the reasons for the rejection. (Havas, 15th)

Amsterdam. According to responsible persons here, the Dutch government will thoroughly study the Dutch-Belgian peace proposal from Germany, carefully examine the current situation, and consult with Belgium. (Haitong Telegraph, 16th)

The Hague. This morning, Dutch newspapers published prominently the news that German Foreign Minister Ribbentrop had given the German response to the peace proposals of the two Dutch and Belgian heads of state to the envoys of the two countries stationed in Germany. The Dutch newspapers pointed out that Britain and France resolutely rejected the peace proposals, so Germany now also talks about the fact that the mediation business has ended. After receiving the news, the Dutch government contacted the Belgian government to exchange views on the current situation. The New Rotterdam Daily believes that readers should not rush to a conclusion on this matter, because Germany rejected the mediation because Britain and France rejected the peace proposals. If Britain and France explained that they did not mean to reject the proposals abruptly, then Germany might not necessarily fail to consider them. (Haitong Telegraph, 16th)

Situation Eases at Dutch-Belgian Border

Paris. Informed sources here said that although the tense situation at the border between Germany and Belgium and the Netherlands has eased, the German troops and military equipment concentrated in the border areas in the past week have not been withdrawn. From a purely military point of view, the German army can still launch at any time, and the threat to Belgium and the Netherlands has not diminished. However, Belgium and the Netherlands have taken the necessary precautions, and their defenses have become stronger day by day. At the same time, the French government has also taken the necessary measures in the border area to cope with any German attempts. Although Germany is still ready to give it a try, its current enemies and future enemies have already prepared and rested, and all things that may succeed by chance are absolutely impossible. Therefore, the hope of its success is greatly reduced. In addition, winter is approaching, and if the country wants to launch something at this time, it will be more difficult. (Havas, 16th)

Belgian Capital. All public buses in the city that were requisitioned by the government were returned in full today, and buses on all routes have been running as usual. (Havas Military, 16th)

Amsterdam. The canal between Amsterdam and the North Sea, which was previously closed for night navigation due to the tense situation from Sunday, has now been reopened. This can be seen as another indication that the Netherlands is gradually becoming quieter. (Reuters, 16th)

Polish Premier Engaged in Activities in England; Talks with British Cabinet Members

London. Since arriving at this inquiry the day before yesterday, General Sikorski, the Prime Minister of Poland, is conducting talks with various members of the British Cabinet. It is reported that the most important issues being discussed are the organization of Polish troops fighting on the Western Front and the relief of Polish refugees. (Havas, 15th)

London. General Sikorski, the Prime Minister of Poland, gave a speech in French at a banquet of the Foreign Correspondents Association here, saying, "From a personal point of view, the current war did not come out of our intentions, and has already transcended the conflict between countries. Whether the principles of law and justice that all mankind should follow can be extended depends on who wins this war. Today, fair observers have felt that all mankind must choose between two different collective lives. One is the way of life expressed by Britain, France, and the United States, and the other can be represented by the horizontal occupation of Austria and Czechoslovakia and the horizontal division of Poland. After my trip to conduct talks with the British authorities, it has been proven that the governments of the two countries have the same views, and their connection is very strong. The Polish army is being reorganized in the territory of Britain and France, and the British and French governments have given great support in spirit and in material. Our team is also cooperating with the strong British fleet. All our sailors are welcomed by their British comrades. It is expected that our land and air forces can fight together with the friendly forces of the Allied countries of Britain and France in a few months. (Havas, 16th)

Large Numbers of German Political Prisoners Arrested

Swiss National Capital. The Sérère City Daily reported that German political police arrested no fewer than 1,000 people yesterday, most of whom were socialists and communists released from concentration camps, as well as monarchists, Christian intellectuals, and Jews, and even National Socialists. More arrests are expected to follow. (Havas, 16th)

Munich. After the bomb explosion at the Bergeru Hotel in Munich, which killed seven people, it has been learned that another person (Michael Shiguode) died of his injuries the day before yesterday. His funeral was held here today, and representatives from the party and government attended the ceremony. There were many spectators. (Haitong Telegraph, 16th)

Puppet Manchukuo Economy Severely Affected by European War; Soybeans Cannot Be Shipped to Germany; Japan and the Soviet Union Prepare to Negotiate

Changchun. After the outbreak of the European War, the economy of "Manchukuo" has been severely affected. Exports of soybeans and their by-products to Germany have now stopped, and many urgently needed materials taken from Germany are also unable to be obtained. Many factories built to install German machinery are now empty. Industry in the territory is also very lacking, and imports are difficult to resume. The negotiations between Changchun and Tokyo on giving priority to Japanese imported goods being shipped into Manchuria have not been successfully completed. The monopolistic system originally intended to expand "Manchukuo's" export trade has become a pie in the sky. All the warehouses north of Dalian are now piled high with goods, relying solely on Japanese consumption, which is not enough to create a balance of foreign trade. Those with knowledge say that shipping soybeans by rail through Siberia to Germany is nonsense. Leaving aside the amount of freight, the lack of vehicles in "Manchukuo" and the Soviet Union is even more of a problem. As for the idea of refining soybean essence and shipping it to Germany, chemists also believe it is impossible, because the ingredients of soybeans cannot be refined into fine particles, making it economically and commercially suitable for transportation on the Siberian Railway. Therefore, what "Manchukuo" is currently encountering is the difficulty that countries around the world have failed to solve for a hundred years. Agricultural authorities are now planning to change agricultural production so that the territory can be self-sufficient and have a surplus to be exported to other countries in exchange for urgently needed industrial products. (Reuters, 16th)

Tokyo. After meeting with Soviet Ambassador Smetanin for 50 minutes yesterday, Japanese Foreign Minister Nomura decided that the agenda of the Chita Conference should be limited to the Nomonhan issue. The Asahi Shimbun said, "The border between 'Manchukuo' and the Soviet Union can be finally demarcated next spring. Negotiations to extend the 1928 Fisheries Agreement for 12 months will also be held soon." (Reuters, 16th)

Tokyo. Japanese Kyushu Daily President Kiyomizu Yoshitaro publicly published a letter yesterday, advocating that Japan should conclude a non-aggression treaty with the Soviet Union, emphasizing that Japan's understanding with the Soviet Union is an absolute prerequisite for realizing its policy towards China. War between Japan and the Soviet Union, or even strained relations, will strengthen the position of Britain and the United States in the Far East. Soviet Foreign People's Commissar Molotov has stated that the Soviet Union is willing to seek understanding with Japan, so the Japanese government should seize the opportunity, actively strive to overthrow the pro-British and pro-Russian traditional principles, and issue a non-aggression treaty with the Soviet Union. If it can be realized, it will not hinder Japan's negotiations with Britain and the United States, but will be enough to make the negotiations easier. (Haitong Telegraph, 16th)

Tokyo. The new Soviet Ambassador, Smetanin, will be received by the Japanese Emperor on November 20 to present his credentials. (Reuters, 16th)

Pan-American Economic Committee Met Yesterday; Welles Gave a Speech

Washington. The Pan-American Economic Committee met here, and US Undersecretary of State Welles first gave a speech, saying, "We are now starting work in an extremely favorable situation. The determination of the American republics to maintain the security and peace of the Western Hemisphere is known to the world." The task of this committee is to propose appropriate measures to stabilize the business relations of the American countries that have been affected by the European War, and at the same time to always find ways to increase the volume of trade between the American countries. I propose to elect a subcommittee to "discuss ways to develop and facilitate business, improve monetary and financial institutions, promote sound production and investment matters, improve transportation and communication methods, and communicate technical knowledge and experiences from all parties to make the most of them." In addition, I also advocate that the American countries conduct negotiations to discuss bilateral business terms to develop trade, and improve the non-competitive agricultural and industrial products of all parties. All American countries have the possibility of using foreign capital to develop natural resources, and all departments of the United States government should cooperate with other American countries in the most friendly spirit." (Havas, 16th)

Finance Heavy Selling Resurges, Morning Foreign Exchange Market Again Shows Sharp Decline

Yesterday morning in the foreign exchange market, the opening price announced by HSBC was flat. The black market for British and American currencies, contrary to the quiet of the previous few days, entered a state of tension again. It was at its lowest around noon, reaching a rate of 5 shillings, 4 pence, 6875. However, by closing time, it had recovered slightly to 5 shillings, 2.25 pence. The morning opened relatively stable, but after 9:30 AM, heavy selling suddenly began. It was estimated that Hong Kong Electric, speculators, and outsiders such as Chase National Bank, the Dutch Bank, and Anda Bank eagerly sold off. Furthermore, due to the spread of unfavorable news that German troops had begun to invade the Dutch border from a certain defense line, and that important British military meetings were discussing countermeasures, it was also heard that German merchants, due to the expansion of the European situation, had wired orders to Hong Kong to sell off. As a result, the selling became more intense, and HSBC's appetite for buying became increasingly weak, leading to a breakdown in support. The American exchange rate almost broke the 9 yuan mark, reaching 8.9375 yuan, and the British pound also rose to 5 shillings, 4 pence, 6875. However, the selling soon subsided slightly, and importers, seeing the low prices, quickly and decisively bought in. HSBC's intention to buy was also strong at this time, causing the market to turn around briefly, dropping to 5 shillings, 3.4375 pence and 8.75 yuan. However, the closing price at noon turned softer again. In the afternoon, due to Japanese banks entering the market to buy, and HSBC's appetite for buying remaining strong, the lowest rate recovered to 5 shillings, 2.25 pence and 8.59375 yuan. After hovering around this level, the market soon closed, with the British pound at 5 shillings, 2.96875 pence and the American exchange rate at 8.6875 yuan, slightly firmer by 0.078125 and 0.125 compared to the previous day. It was heard that the trend of futures was the same as that of spot, but the result was slightly squeezed, with the British pound differing by 0.0625 and the American exchange rate differing by 0.125, equivalent to a monthly interest rate of about 1%. Trading throughout the day was active.

Knowledge for Couples

Hygiene for Married Life in Early Winter

— Co-authored by Yao Chongpei, American Medical Doctor, Venereal Disease Specialist, and Zhan Nianceng

(Clinic) 2nd Floor, China Trust Company, Sichuan Road, Beijing Road

(Hours) 10:00 AM to 6:00 PM, Sunday by Appointment

How many couples in this world unknowingly fall into a miserable hell due to a lack of hygiene! It is a fact that a husband with strong essence and vitality is usually in the dominant position in sexual relations. Although the wife hopes that her husband will always be by her side, she does not always enjoy "that" often. However, when she is at the peak of her passion, she hopes that her husband is strong, virile, and has endurance, so that they can spend their happy life in the harmony of love. This is also the creator's way of rewarding men for improving their health. If a man loses his health due to excessive indulgence and debauchery, he should bear full responsibility. Excessive indulgence and masturbation leading to spermatorrhea are most likely to deplete the reproductive gland fluid, which is the source of our life. Therefore, men who are depleted of essence and vitality are almost certain to suffer from neurasthenia, incomplete development, premature ejaculation, impotence, premature aging, and weak brain and kidney deficiency. At the same time, due to the deficiency and strong desire, it is also most likely to cause impulses in this long winter night, arousing his wife's passion, but often presenting a fleeting pleasure that cannot be satisfied. Page 9

Japan's War in China: Already in a Difficult Situation, Utterly Submissive to the Soviet Union and the United States, Still Hesitant About Ending the War - Important Remarks by Suma

After the newly appointed Director of the Information Department of the Japanese Foreign Ministry, Yakichiro Suma, arrived in Shanghai, he held a special press conference at the Broadway Mansions on the afternoon of the previous day, inviting foreign journalists to answer various questions raised. Suma first stated, "I have been away from the Far East for a long time, and my visit to China this time is to see and hear about the 'New Order in East Asia.'" In response to reporters' inquiries, he said, "Regarding the idea of how to resolve the Sino-Japanese war, the theory of dividing China's spheres of influence between the Soviet Union and Japan is the most ridiculous." When a reporter asked, "Then what is the best option?" he replied, "The best option is to implement the intentions of the statement made by former Japanese Prime Minister Fumimaro Konoe on December 22, 1938."

Soviet-Japanese Pending Issues: Urgent Need for Resolution

When asked, "What efforts will Japan make to improve Soviet-Japanese relations and form a treaty of non-aggression between the two countries?" he replied, "There are no specific steps yet, so there are no preconditions for the Soviet Union and Japan to conclude a treaty." Regarding Soviet-Japanese relations, Suma said, "There are currently some outstanding issues between the two countries that need to be resolved. Tokyo believes that each issue should be resolved step by step, and finally the relations between the two countries can be adjusted." When a reporter asked, "In the current Soviet-Japanese negotiations, is the issue of Soviet aid to China one of the main points?" he replied, "The main outstanding issues in the negotiations are fishing rights, border issues, etc. The discussion of these issues and political disputes are not incorporated into the intentions of the Japanese government." When a reporter asked, "Many people believe that the Soviet government and the Third International are one and the same. Can Japan launch an anti-communist movement while simultaneously concluding a non-aggression treaty with the Soviet Union?" Suma avoided answering directly, saying, "I did not say that Japan will conclude a non-aggression treaty with the Soviet Union. Japan's policy has not changed."

How to End the Sino-Japanese War

Although Suma said that the best way to resolve the Sino-Japanese conflict is to realize Konoe's statement, he failed to clearly state Japan's ultimate determination to withdraw its troops from China, saying, "This depends on future developments and circumstances." Regarding the "New Central Government," Suma said, "There are no accurate reports, as the official establishment date has not been determined. Although there have been news of dates from Tokyo, it is only based on individual perspectives. The reason for the delay in establishment is not due to insufficient preparation of affairs, or because it is not easy to establish, or because it has encountered some obstacles and become deadlocked. The Japanese government is still continuing its established policy to achieve its goals." When a reporter asked, "In your speech, the final withdrawal of Japanese troops from China depends on future developments. Does this mean that Wang Jingwei cannot guarantee to the Chinese people that he can achieve the withdrawal of Japanese troops?" Suma was speechless and only said, "Japan's policy is only based on Konoe's statement. As for what Mr. Wang does or what other parties do, it is none of our concern and should not be stated by Japanese officials." When a reporter asked, "Mr. Wang stated on November 12 of this year that he will seek absolute freedom and independence for China. If there is no way, then he will have to fight to the end. What is your opinion?" Suma considered this question and decided not to answer, saying, "I do not want to discuss any statements from the Chinese side at the moment, including Wang's claims." However, when asked whether "Tokyo is willing to negotiate directly with the National Government or through the mediation of a third country," Suma's answer was affirmative, saying, "There is no such intention at all." When a reporter asked, "Is Japan only supporting Wang Jingwei?" Suma replied, "Japan's support is not limited to any one person, but depends on the claims of their 'regime.' All claims that are in line with Japan's interests will receive broad support."

Japan Exhausted, Submissive to the United States

The discussion then turned to the issue of US-Japan relations. Suma stated, "I have just returned from the United States, so I feel that I know a lot about the United States. I feel that the US government and people, from top to bottom, have never hoped for a deterioration in US-Japan relations, so I believe that US-Japan relations will definitely improve. After returning to my country, this hope has increased even more, because I see that the Japanese government and the Japanese people are eagerly hoping to obtain the understanding of the United States. Although the 594 cases of US protests against Japan have not yet been resolved, Japan should strive to satisfy the United States and resolve them. However, Japan's use of troops in China has reached a very large degree. Under this situation, seeking to resolve the pending issues with the United States will naturally take time. However, Japan's efforts and goodwill will be seen one day." When a reporter asked, "Is it possible for a new US-Japan commercial treaty to be completed before January next year?" Suma admitted that the Japanese government is eager for the conclusion of a new commercial treaty, and said, "If the United States is unwilling to sign a new commercial treaty with Japan, the affected parties will not only be Japan, but the United States will also feel inconvenienced. The Americans should believe this." When a reporter asked, "Can the so-called 'New Order in East Asia' make the United States feel that it does not conflict with its government?" he replied, "American newspapers and magazines have expressed various opinions on this, but the American government and people may not all be die-hards who oppose the 'New Order.' "The US government has made it clear that it is not blind to the progress of the world, and since the entire world, including East Asia, is in turmoil, I believe that the United States does not want to run counter to the progress of the situation and remain in a stage of blindness."

On the morning of the 12th, they drove away the Japanese troops in Wuhe and Jing, and took advantage of the victory to launch a fierce attack on Shiwan. They continued to recapture Shuanglin. Also, Chongqing, 15th – Chinese troops in western Zhejiang adopted a comprehensive tactic, inflicting heavy blows on the Japanese troops. Chinese troops in the Chongde, Wuxing, and Tongxiang areas, after encircling the Japanese troops from the night of the 9th, engaged in fierce battles in Lutou, northwest of Tongxiang, Wuzhen, Puxian, Tongxiang, Xinshi, northwest of Jiaxing, and along the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway in Chang'an and Xiashi. After being pressured by the Chinese troops, the Japanese troops fled in different directions. More than 40 Japanese troops, transported by civilian boats and motorboats, fled to Linghu (part of Wuxing). Another group of 50 Japanese troops, transported by motorboats and civilian boats from Xinshi, fled to Qianjin Market. The Chinese troops are pursuing them.

Japanese Troops Invading Danyang Completely Annihilated, New Fourth Army Fights Fiercely Southwest of Danyang, Killing More Than 270 Japanese Soldiers, Japan Acknowledges Active Chinese Troops in the Lower Yangtze River

In order to cooperate with the new anti-Japanese situation after the great victory of the Chinese troops in northern Hunan, the New Fourth Army and the Jiangnan Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, which are densely concentrated behind the Japanese troops along the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway, are constantly carrying out guerrilla tactics of ambushes and flank attacks. As a result, the scope of activities of the Japanese troops in the occupied areas has been shrinking day by day, and they are suffering greatly. According to visitors from Danyang, on the morning of the 8th of this month, more than 100 Japanese soldiers, carrying light military weapons, invaded Yanling Town (40 li southwest of Danyang) from Baoyan (27 li south of Danyang) with great fanfare.

Fierce Fighting, Japanese Ultimately Encircled

After receiving intelligence reports, the X Battalion of the First Regiment and Commander Wang of the Second Regiment of the New Fourth Army personally led the X Battalion to make strict arrangements to gather the troops in Jiuli Town and Majia Village, west of Yanling, forming a strong encirclement. A fierce battle immediately broke out with the Japanese troops. The sound of gunfire and artillery shook dozens of li. Because the New Fourth Army received the assistance of the people, accurate intelligence, familiarity with and advantage of the terrain, and the destruction of transportation on roads around, the Japanese troops could not be reinforced in a continuous stream. In addition, with rich combat experience (the army has experienced more than 300 battles of all sizes), a clear understanding of the anti-Japanese war, and a hundredfold courage, everyone fought bravely, with one person acting as ten, and charged valiantly. Although the Japanese troops relied on sophisticated weapons, most of them were eventually annihilated.

Japanese Completely Annihilated in One Day and One Night

Subsequently, more than 200 Japanese soldiers from Danyang and Baitu Town came to reinforce. The X Battalion of the Second Regiment of the New Fourth Army also rushed to the scene, and a fierce battle, rarely seen in Jiangnan in the past two years, unfolded. The battle started on the morning of the 8th and lasted until the morning of the 9th, a total of 28 hours. As a result, all the Japanese troops were annihilated, with more than 270 killed, dozens wounded, six light and heavy machine guns captured, three grenade launchers, more than 160 rifles, three Japanese soldiers captured, and countless other military supplies. In this battle, the army also heroically sacrificed 50 or 60 people and wounded 40 or 50 people. This battle can be described as a remarkable feat of the army on the Jiangnan battlefield.

Fujita Acknowledges Active Chinese Troops

According to Japanese sources yesterday, Lieutenant General Fujita, the newly appointed commander of the Shanghai area, gave a speech to a group of foreign journalists on the 15th, acknowledging the activity of the Chinese troops, making it impossible to establish "security." Fujita said that the lower Yangtze River area is the most important place for politics, economy, and military affairs in central China, and the establishment of "security" there is the most urgent task. However, there are still regular Chinese troops and guerrilla units that launch attacks from time to time, disrupting "security." Therefore, the Japanese army intends to exert all its efforts to "eliminate" these troops in order to establish "security." However, the Chinese side firmly believes that this kind of attempt by the Japanese side will ultimately be futile.

Japanese Troops on North Jiangxi Road Suddenly Intensify Inspection

Those Blocked Numbered 70 to 80, The Exit Seems to Be More Relaxed.

At the two gaps on North Jiangxi Road, the intersection of Wenjian Shi Road and Haining Road, the Japanese troops guarding the posts suddenly paid special attention to pedestrians entering on the afternoon of yesterday. In addition to taking the passes and verifying the photos and ages one by one, they also observed whether the state and clothing were different or consistent. If the photos were not recent, or the clothing in the photos did not match what was worn, they were considered suspicious, and the passes were immediately torn up. As a result, as many as seventy or eighty pedestrians were blocked for no reason. The tension was unprecedented. However, the two gaps seemed to be more relaxed.

Japanese Troops Land in Beihai, Shanghai Ships Temporarily Do Not Call, Taikoo Jinan Wheel Sailed South Yesterday and Was Implemented, South China Route Encountered Another Major Blow

Since the fall of Guangzhou, various shipping companies have opened up a new route for coastal defense in Guangzhou Bay. According to the English-language "Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury," the British Consulate General will protest to "Mayor Chuan Xiaolan" regarding the fact that a British person was driving a car through the intersection of Difeng Road and Daxilu Road last night, and was allegedly shot at once by a policeman of the "Special Municipal Government" "on traffic duty" because he ignored the signal issued. The foreign community in the city is quite resentful of this shooting case. A large number of armed police officers on the road are already trying to seize the activities of the Public Security Bureau of the Public Concession on the roads and sidewalks outside the concession. Now, driving to that area feels unsafe.

Name of British Person Not Yet Announced

The name of the British person has not been announced. He was driving a car along Difeng Road last night and drove past a policeman on the road wearing a black winter uniform. When the car passed the intersection, a shot was heard and the bullet flew past the car. The British person accelerated away. The shooter seemed to be standing on the sidewalk rather than the "police officer on traffic duty." Later, someone asked the police why he fired. He replied, "Because the person in the car saw the police signal and did not stop the car."

British Military Authorities Demand Explanation

According to the Continental Daily, a British person was driving a car from Difeng Road into Maggie Road yesterday (15th) night, and was shot at by a false policeman because he did not see the traffic signal from the "Special Municipal Government" police. The name of the British person was not disclosed last night. The Jing'an Temple Police Station did not receive any news about this matter, but the British military authorities have notified the "Special Municipal Government Police Bureau" to demand an explanation.

Did Not See Signal, Suddenly Heard Gunshot

The British person was driving south along Difeng Road from the north. Near Daxilu Road, he slowed down and continued to drive forward when a policeman from the "Special Municipal Government" did not make a traffic signal gesture. As soon as the car passed the intersection of Haig Road and entered Maggie Road, a gunshot was suddenly heard, and the bullet flew past the car, luckily missing. He continued to drive forward and reported to the British Military Headquarters.

British Consulate Protest to Be Filed Today

Last night's final news was that the British Consulate was waiting for a detailed report from the Bureau of Public Works regarding the shooting of British residents by false police the night before and could file a protest with the false mayor by this afternoon at the latest. It was also learned that the British military's question to the false police bureau had not been answered as of last night, but the British military had ascertained the number of the false police officer who fired the shot and had notified the false police bureau. The name of the British resident who was attacked will not be released to avoid accidents, but it is known that he is a member of the Shanghai International Volunteer Corps.

Street Children Being Sheltered

Many Are War Orphans

The Shanghai Municipal Council is now making every effort to arrange for street children. According to the police department, in October, 34 vagrant children who lingered on the streets and children who specialized in opening car doors to solicit rewards were taken in by the police. Most of these children have been living on the streets for two years, sleeping in the open, which is very miserable. Most of them are orphaned children after the "August 13th" battle, alone and begging. The Municipal Council has already been aware of this, so it recently established a street children's shelter at No. 190 Ningbo Road to accommodate these orphaned beggars. There are now 50 beggars in the shelter. Therefore, the beggar children who used to be found opening car doors and soliciting rewards from passengers at various wharves and streets are no longer found now.

Fujita Shows Inner Distress to Foreign Journalists, Unwilling to Offend Soviet Union and United States, Difficult to Say When Sino-Japanese War Will End

—Opening Up the Interior Is Also Lip Service and Not Substantial—

According to the North China Daily News, Lieutenant General Fujita, commander of the Japanese army in the Shanghai area, stated at a reception for foreign journalists at his official residence in Jiangwan yesterday (15th) afternoon that the Japanese army would avoid meaningless conflicts with the Soviet Union as much as possible in order to contribute to world peace. He earnestly hoped that after a reasonable and understanding approach was achieved to resolve the long-standing issues between the United States and Japan, relations between the two countries would greatly improve. As for the revocation of restrictions on trade and travel in the interior by people of third countries, he could not give any definite guarantees. The issue of allowing unrestricted residence in Nanshi is currently under serious study by the Japanese military authorities.

Opening Up the Interior Is Hopeless

Fujita replied to a large number of written questions submitted by reporters in advance, expressing his opinion that the military equipment and other war materials supplied by Europe to Chongqing have certainly decreased due to the outbreak in Europe. Fujita also assured reporters that within the possible scope of military needs, restrictions on trade and travel in the interior by foreigners will be gradually eased. However, this easing must not hinder military operations. He could not say when the easing would be implemented, as this point depends on the deployment of the Japanese army and the situation in the enemy's camp.

Difficult to Predict Future of War Against China

When asked how extensive the activities of the guerrillas in the Yangtze River basin and near Nanjing were, Fujita replied that the Japanese troops occupying these areas had repeatedly contacted the guerrillas, but the guerrillas are now gradually ineffective. After the recruitment period, peace and order will be restored. Because there are wars on both sides, travelers are quite dangerous, so restrictions on travel and commerce in these areas are unavoidable. He could not say how long the Sino-Japanese war would last. Whether Japan has continued military objectives in China depends entirely on future circumstances.

Japanese in China Are of Uneven Quality

US-Japan relations have improved slightly. If both sides have a thorough discussion of the pending issues, he believes that the differences that still exist can be resolved, and the relations between the two countries can have a clearer atmosphere. Before Fujita got up, he also discussed various issues related to China and Japan with the reporters. He asked how many of the reporters present had lived in Japan, and then asked if, in their opinion, Japanese people were unpleasant people. One reporter replied that Japanese people in Japan were indeed like that, but many Japanese people in China were not. Fujita laughed when he heard this, saying that unfortunately, the Japanese people in China are of uneven quality.

Zhejiang Province Establishes Oil Collection Network for Tung Oil Purchases

Province Divided into Three Regions, Oil Stations Established at Key Points

Zhejiang Province's purchase of tung oil was previously contracted by the provincial government with the Central Trust Bureau, and the Oil Tea Cotton Silk Management Office was entrusted to undertake the work. The purchase started on October 11. In order to facilitate the sale of oil by farmers and merchants, a province-wide oil collection network has been established. Except for the counties in the war zone, the oil-producing areas in eastern Zhejiang are divided into three regions: Jinquyan, Ningshaotai, and Wenchu. Within each region, oil collection stations are established at key points according to the production and transportation conditions to directly purchase oil. For counties with a large amount of oil production but without oil collection stations, the oil collection stations entrust local banks, cooperative treasuries, trading shops, and cooperatives to purchase oil at appropriate locations. Counties without the above institutions may entrust registered and qualified oil dealers to purchase on their behalf. The price of oil is uniformly set at 50 yuan per market dan (100 catties). Oil-filled tin containers are subsidized at 1 yuan per market dan, for a total of 51 yuan. The Zhejiang Provincial Government also promulgated a provisional outline of measures for the control and transportation of tung oil and ordered it to be followed.

To Ship Goods to Malaya, Local Customs Must Be Registered, Restrictions on 34 Kinds of Goods Are a Controlled Policy, Non-Sterling Group Goods Must Be Approved

Since the Malayan government promulgated measures to restrict the import of 34 kinds of goods this year, various domestic goods factories in this city, due to their failure to fully understand the reasons for this, have successively written to the Shanghai General Federation of Chinese Industries, requesting the association to inquire on their behalf. The association, considering that the matter concerned the entire issue of domestic goods, forwarded the letter to Mr. Gao Shiheng, the overseas domestic goods inspection representative, requesting him to investigate the matter clearly and reply to relieve the public's doubts. Now Mr. Gao has replied in a letter, saying that after the Malayan government announced the restriction on the import of 34 kinds of goods, its purpose was to control foreign exchange and prevent the flight of funds. Any country outside the Sterling Group that wants to import these 34 kinds of goods must first request registration with the local customs. Only after approval can the goods be allowed to be imported. At present, these application procedures are not difficult, but just require one more procedure. Importers here have pre-processed these procedures for goods shipped from Shanghai before importing them. As for future changes, it is difficult to predict. All countries are now paying attention to control work, and regardless of the import and export of foreign exchange and goods, they are building barriers. We should pay attention to this.

Labor Negotiations Interrupted Again

Factory Still Plans to Find a Solution

Loading Cargo Between Shanghai and Shipu

Carrying Passengers Between Shanghai and Zhenhai

Regarding the issue of shortening the shipping route and voyage of the Shanghai-Ningbo line, although it was previously planned that the Fook Line would be the first to try a method where passengers going to Ningbo from Shanghai would be transferred, and cargo would not be transferred temporarily. Mr. Yu Qiaqing Talks About the Truth of Coal Briquette Price Drop

Da Mao Coal Briquette Factory is Purely Operated by Chinese Merchants

The Purpose is to Stabilize Market Prices for the Benefit of the Common People

Regarding the recent drop in coal briquette prices in this city, Mr. Yu Qiaqing told a Daguan News Agency reporter yesterday that coal briquettes are an important fuel for residents of this city, and are particularly closely related to the interests of the lower and middle classes. A few months ago, coal prices soared. Anthracite coal is used by factories and ships, and white coal is needed by middle and upper class families to ward off the cold, so the impact is relatively light. However, coal briquettes are a necessity of daily life and have the same nature as rice. The price increase to four yuan and five jiao per dan (equivalent to ten yuan per ton) has become unbearable for the people. He consulted with coal merchant Mr. Zhang and others to set up a factory. The factory is located at the original site of the Jardine Matheson sugar godown in Pudong. Moreover, it is well known to people in the coal industry that the white coal dust used to make coal briquettes is not a Japanese product. Furthermore, the raw materials used by the factory are entirely shipped from French Annam to Shanghai, which is also a fact. After the factory was established, prices immediately dropped, reducing the burden on ordinary people. The current market price of coal briquettes has been stabilized at sixty-three yuan per ton and three yuan and five jiao per dan, which greatly benefits the livelihood of the common people. The rumor that the products of the Da Mao factory are Japanese coal briquettes is likely due to jealousy from competitors. This report aims to clarify the truth and distinguish between right and wrong.

Owner of Garden Villa at Avenue Joffre Sues for Eviction; Owner Appeals to the High Court, Retrial Yesterday

A large garden villa at 1877 Avenue Joffre is the property of Tao Huayu Fang, the wife of Tao Jiayao, the former governor of Jiangxi Province, the former head of the National Water Conservancy, and the current chairman of the China Funeral Home, who is from Jiangxi. The Tao family used to live there. During the August 13th Incident, the entire Tao family moved to 6 Lane 753 Haig Road. After the war broke out, the property was entrusted to the Tong An Company for rent. In October of the 26th year of the Republic (1937), the Central Mint rented the house from the Tong An Company to use as an office location at a monthly rent of four hundred yuan. At that time, both parties

Signed a lease agreement

But stipulated that the shortest period was three months. Around October of last year, Mrs. Tao sold the villa to a Westerner named Qiaoqi (transliteration), and at the same time terminated the lease with the Central Mint, ordering them to move out. Because the Central Mint refused to move out, the Tao family could not hand over the house to Qiaoqi according to the sales contract, so the Tao family compensated Qiaoqi one thousand five hundred yuan and cancelled the house sale contract. The lease

Term expired

The landlord, Accountant Dali, refused to continue the lease. The Tao family urgently needed to move, and again ordered the Central Mint to move out so that they could take back the house for their own residence. As a result, due to the Central Mint's opposition, in April of this year, Tao Huayu Fang, the wife of Tao Jiayao, the owner of the villa, came forward and appointed lawyers Li Guozhen and Li Yujun to file a lawsuit in the Second Special Court's Civil Division against Tan Songtao, the legal representative of the Central Mint.

Seeking eviction

And compensation for damages of one thousand five hundred yuan. Judge Dong Zi Guan opened the court for trial. The defendant, Tan Songtao from the Central Mint, was represented by lawyer Ma Shouhua. The defendant argued that they had rented the house from the Tong An Company, and the subject of the lawsuit was inconsistent. The plaintiff first sold the house and then wanted to take it back for their own residence, so the objectives were inconsistent, opposing the eviction. The plaintiff's

House sale dispute

Resulted in compensation of one thousand five hundred yuan for breach of contract, which the defendant should not be responsible for. The three-month lease term stipulated in the contract had already passed, so the lease was indefinite. The defendant should have the benefit of the lease, and the plaintiff's request for eviction was unreasonable. As a result, the first instance judgment rejected the plaintiff's claim. Tao Huayu Fang was not satisfied and appealed to the Civil Division of the Third High Court. The result was rejected. She then appealed to the Shanghai Special District Branch of the Supreme Court for a third trial. The Shanghai Branch of the Supreme Court has now reviewed the entire case file and ruled that the portion of the appeal concerning compensation for damages is rejected, and the appeal for the eviction portion is remanded to the Third High Court

For retrial

The Third High Court received the judgment and case file. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xia Jinde, accompanied by Judge Tong, opened the court for trial. Both the appellant and the appellee were represented by lawyers. Both sides made their arguments, each with sufficient reasons. The court then questioned the appellant Tao Huayu Fang in detail about whether she was the spouse of Tao Jiayao, and announced that they would

Set a date for witnesses and continue the debate.
