Car Driver Recognized the Truth

Car Drove into the Police Station

Jiang Fulin, a native of Changzhou, who specializes in kidnapping women, kidnapped two female workers, Shi Sunshi (20 years old, resident of 5 Qianxingfang, Binlang Road) and Zheng Lishi (19 years old), in front of the Shenxin Textile Factory at 4 PM on the 12th of this month and hid them in the home of his accomplice, Mei Yaozong, at 3872 Daxuli, Ma-bai Road. The next day, they led them to the Zhonghua Hotel on Xujiahui Road and locked them in a room for illicit purposes. At 10:30 PM on the 15th, the two kidnappers Jiang and Mei called a rental car from the Zhongshan Automobile Company on Father Jin Road and tricked the two victims into getting into the car, intending to take a boat from Yichang Road Bridge to Changzhou to sell them. Fortunately, the rental car driver Mao Guisheng recognized the truth and, without saying a word, drove the car into the Putuo Road Police Station to report. After an investigation by Hua detective Chen Xianrong, the defendant Jiang Fulin confessed to the kidnapping and sale of the victims. Yesterday morning, the police escorted the defendants to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court and prosecuted them for crimes such as interfering with family harmony. Judge Liu Yugui concluded the trial and ordered them to be detained pending judgment.

Missing Rental Car Driver Case; Police Conduct Strict Investigation; Notified Water Police to Assist in the Search; Bullets Have Been Examined, No Record Found

On the morning of the 14th, a rental car with a missing driver was discovered on Race Course Road, Longmen Road. There were bloodstains on the driver's seat cushion, and two bullets were found in the car. It was clear that the driver had been killed. The Concession Police Department is making every effort to search for the driver's body.

So far, no body has been found. Yesterday, it was learned that the police have asked the Water Police to assist in the search, fearing that the driver's body may have been sunk in the Huangpu River. According to the police's speculation, the rental car was hired for criminal activity. After the illegal act was completed, the criminals realized that the driver knew too much and took the extreme measure of silencing him. This can be inferred from the bloodstains on the driver's seat, the bullets in the car, and the driver's disappearance. It was also learned that the bullet inspection experts at the Public Security Bureau, upon

Examination results, the bullets found in the car had no previous record. The rental car belongs to the Japanese-owned Xinxing Automobile Company at 170 Wusong Road, Hongkou. At 5:30 PM on the 13th, the company received a phone call to rent a car. Driver Zhao Shanxing (20 years old) drove to the south of Suzhou Creek. However, the car was not returned after a long wait, so the company notified the police. After a search, the mysterious empty car was discovered the next morning on Race Course Road, Longmen Road.

Female Corpse Discovered on Xinji Bang Road, Hongkou

At approximately 9 AM yesterday, someone passing near Xinji Bang, Dongyouheng Road, Hongkou, saw a female corpse on a vacant lot and immediately reported it to the local police station. Detective number one was dispatched to investigate and sent the female corpse to the Tongren Hospital. An examination revealed that the female corpse was in her twenties. The right temple had a knife wound with a very deep gash, and the brain matter had spilled out. The left arm bone was broken. It appeared she had been murdered. She was wearing a black qipao, a beige undershirt, white cotton trousers, yellow silk stockings, and gray shoes. After an examination by the doctor, the corpse was transferred to the morgue for further examination.

Owner of Le'an Fang, Avenue Joffre, Shows Consideration for Tenants

The houses in Le'an Fang on Avenue Joffre are managed by the British-owned Taylor & Riley. In February of this year, Taylor & Riley notified all tenants that the rent would be increased by 30%. The tenants strongly refused, arguing that this was an extraordinary period and that they had all come to seek refuge and could not afford such an increase. Later, Taylor & Riley voluntarily reduced the increase to 10%, but the tenants still refused to accept and deposited the rent due in court, which was approved, leading to a stalemate until now. The day before yesterday, Taylor & Riley suddenly had a change of heart and withdrew the rent from the court, canceling the rent increase. The tenants were so grateful for Taylor & Riley's consideration that they sent a letter of thanks. The rent increase dispute, which had lasted for a year, thus came to an end.

Carelessness at the Tongxing Cotton Mill

The Tongxing Cotton Mill at 1433 Yichang Road, Gordon Road, Shanghai West, was suddenly engulfed in flames at approximately 7 PM last night. Thick smoke billowed everywhere, and the fire was raging. The fire brigade rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm and tried their best to put out the fire. The fire was finally extinguished in two hours. As a result, dozens of bales of cotton were burned, and the loss was minor.

Lin Fengmian's Personal Art Exhibition Opens Today

At the Aurora University Auditorium

Lin Fengmian, the former principal of the Hangzhou Art Academy, moved with the entire faculty and students to Guixi, Jiangxi, after the outbreak of the Shanghai-Hangzhou line war. Later, they moved to Yuanling, Hunan. Last year, he resigned from his position and stayed in the countryside of Hunan, dedicating himself to painting. He came to Shanghai this spring and held a personal art exhibition at the French General Association in May, which was well received by the Western press. At that time, most of the visitors were foreigners in this port, and a large number of works were sold. Art circles in this port felt that many Chinese did not have the opportunity to see the exhibition, so they consulted with Mr. Lin and arranged for him to hold another art exhibition at the Aurora University Auditorium on Luba Road for four days, from today to the 20th. The works on display are richer than the last time, totaling approximately 200 pieces, all created during the Anti-Japanese War. Among them, dozens of pieces are based on scenery and folk life from various parts of Hunan, and some are stage scenes depicted by Lin when watching Chinese old dramas, which are full of humor. Lin's works are purely Chinese paintings, and the tools he uses, such as paper, brushes, and pigments, are the same as those used by previous Chinese painters. However, his style and format are mostly unique and completely break away from the stereotypes of traditional Chinese painting. His brushstrokes are simple and vigorous, and his coloring is sparse and clear. The picture is not complicated, but the charm is naturally revealed, which is quite similar to the so-called Impressionist Western paintings. This work has revolutionary significance in the development of Chinese painting art. The exhibition is open from 10 AM to 7 PM, and tickets cost 2 yuan.

Spring and Autumn

YMCA Sponsors Student Service Society: Used Books and Stationery Can Be Consigned, 10% Commission Deducted Upon Sale

— New Dream

In today's era of rising prices and increasingly difficult living standards, students from families with even slightly better financial situations understand the hardship their parents face in raising tuition fees. When it comes to all the necessary stationery and books needed in school, they can practice frugality to show consideration for their parents. At the same time, the Shanghai Christian Men's and Women's YMCA has recognized this need, so they recently established a Student Service Society.

The Student Service Society is located at 999 Jing'an Temple Road, in the Women's YMCA. The day before yesterday afternoon, to learn about the situation of this service society, I made a special visit. It was in a row of bungalows to the left of the Women's YMCA building, together with the Household Goods Exchange, occupying only a corner of the room. On a long table were dozens of used books, and there was also a bookshelf, which was also full of used books.

At another small writing desk sat a staff member, engrossed in writing. I explained my purpose and chatted with him for a while. It is said that the reason why the Men's and Women's YMCA decided to establish this Student Service Society is to promote thrift, practice conserving material resources, trade books and supplies, and serve students throughout the city. The scope of service includes students' daily books, stationery, and all daily necessities, except for impractical, broken, or damaged items, which are not eligible for service.

If students from various schools have used books, stationery, or daily necessities that are no longer suitable for use but are not damaged, they can directly deliver them to the Student Service Society for display and sale. The price can be set by the owner of the goods, but the service society has the right to re-evaluate the price with the consent of the owner. Once the consigned items are sold, the service society will issue a notice at the end of the month, and the owner can go to collect the proceeds of the sale. The service society will deduct 10% of the price as a handling fee. If the owner can contribute more as a donation, that is especially welcome. This handling fee, after deducting office expenses, will be entirely donated to the Shanghai Christian Men's and Women's YMCA Relief Society as student relief funds.

The length of time for which items are consigned will be determined by the service society. If the consigned items cannot be sold or have been consigned for too long, they will notify the owner, who can retrieve them with the receipt issued upon delivery. If the owner still wants to continue consigning, they must re-register. If the owner does not retrieve the goods after the deadline after receiving the notice, the service society has the right to freely mark them down and auction them off, but the proceeds from the auction, after deducting 20% as a handling fee, will still belong to the owner.

Consignment of goods is not limited to students. Manufacturers who want to entrust the Student Service Society to sell their goods are also welcome. However, there are other methods for them, and the above-mentioned provisions do not apply. Currently, the Student Service Society is in its initial stage and is making every effort to promote the society's affairs and is starting to solicit students from various schools to join in cooperation. If possible, in the future, sales outlets may be set up in schools with large student populations, and the methods will be exactly the same as those of a retail department. Indeed, amidst rising prices, the prices of books and stationery have also repeatedly increased. Many parents cannot afford the burden of their children not attending school, and the YMCA's establishment of this service society is also a need of the times, because while it directly enables students to conserve material resources, it indirectly reduces the burden on parents. It is hoped that all young students in Shanghai will join in cooperation so that the Student Service Society can achieve results that exceed expectations in the future.

China's Aircraft Manufacturing Plant

— Jin Ji

According to an American expert who is about to fly from Chongqing, speaking to a Chinese reporter in Hong Kong: Somewhere in southwestern China, there is now an aircraft manufacturing plant built by the Chinese government itself, with more than two thousand technicians and a capital of two million. This plant was entirely established by the Chinese government as part of its plan to develop aviation.

Many hardworking young Chinese technicians, under the guidance of fifteen American aircraft manufacturing experts, are constantly working diligently in the factory. In order to avoid becoming a target for air raids, the constructed factory buildings are all hidden in dense forests and have good air defense facilities. In 1933, the factory was roughly outlined in Hangzhou. By 1934, it was able to manufacture aircraft and supply them to the government.

When the war broke out, the factory was close to the front line and was the first to be attacked by air, but the losses were reported to be small. The factory then began to move to Nanjing and then to Hankou. Finally, 180 transport vehicles were used to carry everything from Hankou to the southwest. Although the factory technicians and staff experienced several scares and difficulties, they were still enthusiastic about their work and showed no resentment.

The factory is now located in the countryside, far from large cities, but general transportation is still convenient. If it needs to be moved again, it will not be difficult. The expert also said that the factory's equipment is no less inferior to that of current American aircraft factories. We estimate that the total construction cost of the factory buildings would be about 700,000 yuan. If a similar aircraft factory were to be built in the United States, it would cost at least US$2.5 million. In addition, there are 21 small dormitories specially designed and constructed for American technicians and a clinic with 81 beds.

Because it concerns military secrets, it is not possible to announce how many products the factory has recently produced, but generally speaking, the results must be good, which is foreseeable. The population near the factory is not very large, only about three thousand five, but the output of materials that can be supplied to the factory is considerable. In the past eight months, the expert has flown between the United States and the area 27 times.

(Translated from the North China Daily News)

Be Careful of Fire

— Dong Er

"Fire! Fire!" Striking headlines are published on the social news pages, with terrible records of people jumping from buildings and becoming disabled, or even more tragically, being buried in the fire. Winter is the season most prone to fires. People go to bed early because of the cold and ignore the smallest spark. Heating with stoves causes a prairie fire. Especially now, when there are too many people in too little space, how many families are crammed into each residence? One wing is rented out to three households; half a floor is divided into two families. As a result, front, back, left, and right are almost all worlds of coal stoves. And the boundaries are all old, thin pine boards, which have been smoked by coal stoves for a long time. Once a fire starts, it is truly unimaginable!

"Be careful of fire! Be careful!" At the same time, we hear such shouts in the streets and alleys.

Being a night watchman in Shanghai is just a humble job of asking each household for some tips at the end of the month. However, in the dead of night, when everyone is dreaming sweet dreams in a warm bed, they brave the wind and cold, circling through every dark alley, touching every household's back door, knocking on the clapper, and shouting, "Be careful of fire," serving for the safety of people's lives and property. We must thank them for this arduous work.

Therefore, when we wake up from a dream in the middle of the night and hear the shout "Be careful of fire," we should check whether there is a risk of fire around us. Moreover, waking up in the middle of the night is also a time for introspection. The sound of the clapper is a warning of a fire in one's conscience, because the "isolated island" is a place to "be careful of fire!"

After the Rain, the Sky Clears

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 17: Learning Fieldwork in a New Realm for Reporters, Studying Domestic Affairs in a Small Practice Field at School

This small travel agency at Soochow University has an employee stationed there by the China Travel Service. Because the school has more than 5,000 people, personnel matters are inevitably complicated, so a trust service society was organized. There are many kinds of services, including a small bank, a small store, a small printing press, etc., and there is also a small travel agency. Although there is only one employee in this small travel agency, he is very busy. Because although most of the students at Soochow University are from Jiangsu, there are also many people from other provinces. Especially from Zhejiang Province, and the next most are from Anhui Province. Even people from Sichuan and Guangdong Provinces are coming and going every day, either teachers and students returning to their hometowns, or large groups of students traveling out. Even elementary school students who are sent to study in Europe and the United States can be handled by this travel agency attached to the school. In addition, today is Saturday, which is considered the busiest day. Some people want to take the Beijing-Shanghai Railway home to visit their families, some want to return to eastern and western Zhejiang via the Suzhou-Jiaxing Road, and even those who are not far from Suzhou and take a small motorboat or long-distance bus for only one or two stops entrust this travel agency to handle it, and the travel agency can handle it properly for you. Originally, if you want to travel somewhere, how many people there are, and where the destination is, just make a phone call to the travel agency, and the travel agency will prepare the tickets for you, or send someone to deliver them to you, or you can pick them up yourself. Fortunately, this travel agency is just outside the dormitory, attached to the trust service society, occupying only a small room. You have to pass in front of it every day when you go to school. When the time comes, the travel agency will make a phone call to the train station, bus station, or small steamer wharf, telling them how many tickets have been sold and asking them to reserve that many seats, which is also very convenient. As for the small bank in the trust service society, it is truly small but complete. There is a savings department, a remittance department, a custody department, and a current account department. With such an organization, it is very convenient. Initially, for example, at the beginning of the spring and autumn semesters, when students pay their tuition, they also pay it to this small bank. Students who bring extra money can also deposit it in this bank. Also, if there are any payments of money, you can open a current account, and they will give you a small checkbook. When you want to pay for something, you fill out a small check, and people will also believe you. Because at that time, no one was willing to write a bad check. As long as you write a bad check once, you will lose your lifelong credit, especially in school, where everyone is young! (203)

A Kirin School Grand Assembly: Dedicated to the Refugee Relief Association

— Only Me

On September 1st, I wrote an article in this publication entitled "Suggestions to the Disaster Relief Authorities to Hold a Kirin School Grand Assembly." Now I hear that this ideal will become a reality. The Refugee Relief Association has tentatively scheduled to hold charity performances for the refugees at the Renxin Theater from the 28th to the 30th of this month for three days. The last day will be based on my suggestion to hold a Kirin School Grand Assembly, but their proposed "Kirin School Grand Assembly" is a joint performance by Zhou Xinfang (麒麟童, aka The Kirin Child) and his disciples, and does not include all Kirin School laosheng (old male role) performers. Therefore, in terms of the playbill, what I proposed earlier will not be suitable for this charity performance. Now, based on the actors they have tentatively decided on, I will re-draft the playbill as follows:

Li Ruchun (Jie Zitui): Burning Mianshan Mountain

Yu Zongying (Ma Chao), Wang Fuying (Zhang Fei): Two Generals

Yang Baotong (Xu Ce): Xu Ce Runs the City

Gao Baisui (Guan Yu)

Zhou Xinfang (Wei Yan), Chen Hefeng (Huang Zhong): Battle of Changsha

Wang Shaolou (Gao Chong): Picking the Hua Che

Li Ruchun (Xiang Bo)

Chen Hefeng (Zhang Liang), Zhou Xinfang (Fan Zeng), Gao Baisui (Xiang Yu), Yang Bintong (Liu Bang), Wang Fuying (Fan Kuai): Hongmen Banquet

The actors in the above playbill are all played by Zhou Xinfang and his disciples. Each person almost plays two plays. In terms of the plays, they are all individual masterpieces. Zhou Xinfang's "Battle of Changsha" is now as popular as "Chasing Han Xin," and his portrayal of Wei Yan is even more unique. This play will surely attract audiences. The finale, "Hongmen Banquet," brings together Kirin School disciples, which can be described as an unprecedented creation. Zhou Xinfang has repeatedly wanted to play Fan Zeng, and this time his wish has come true. In the play "Hongmen Banquet," Fan Zeng occupies a very important position. The personality of this person is difficult to depict, and only Zhou Xinfang can play it successfully. Chen Hefeng is best at playing xiaosheng (young male role) plays, and playing Zhang Liang is just right. Others such as Gao Baisui's Xiang Yu and Wang Fuying's Fan Kuai are known for their superb skills, so this play is a perfect match. If it can be performed, it will surely be a sensation. However, the above playbill can only be performed for 250 minutes, because the actors are limited to Kirin School members, so it is impossible to lengthen it. In my humble opinion, it would be better to invite Kirin School laosheng performers who are not listed in the Kirin School, such as Wang Chunbai and Xu Hongpei, to participate together, which will not only strengthen the lineup but also make the playbill more exciting. In terms of time, adding one or two plays can be performed for more than six hours, which is a perfect plan. I wonder what the gentlemen of the Refugee Relief Association think?

A Meeting with Tang Huaiqiu

— Hua

Tang Huaiqiu has come to Shanghai. On the night of his arrival in Shanghai, he went to the Xuan Palace Theater to watch his daughter Ruoqing's "Regret of the Late Ming Dynasty." When I first discovered him, even we old friends who met every day during the Carlton period almost didn't recognize him. He was wearing dark glasses and had a thick mustache. After only a year apart, this "young father" had actually aged.

That day, because he didn't want to miss this sensational "Regret of the Late Ming Dynasty," after shaking hands, we agreed to talk again the next day and then separated.

The next day, Tang Huaiqiu, who was standing in front of me backstage at Xuan Palace, had regained his youthful and talkative appearance from two years ago. I pretended to point at his mustache, and he grabbed my hand and whispered in my ear as if he were acting:

"My old man doesn't have a beard yet, and the son is keeping this..." He touched his bare upper and lower lips, "It seems a little embarrassing, right?" Although he pretended to be whispering, his voice was still very loud, and the actors in the dressing room couldn't help but laugh.

Tang Ruoqing was just putting on makeup. He turned around and looked at his father and smiled at the mirror. He said to me:

"I was reminded of something. A few days ago, there was a 'Nanguo Entertainment Scene' in your newspaper that said that Ruoying and I were at odds with our father. In fact, the incident at 'China Travel' in Hong Kong was very complicated, and the outside world cannot understand the surface reasons. But I have one sentence I can say, which is that the blame should not be entirely placed on my father. This time my sister came to Shanghai to study, and because I have been away from Shanghai for two years, I also wanted to take this opportunity to come and have some fun, which caused the outside world to say that Ruoying and I were at odds with our father. Now that Dad is back, that is the factual answer."

At that moment, several old friends were urging Tang Huaiqiu to also guest-star in a play at Xuan Palace, but the old actor used a diversion tactic and began to tell a story.

We had heard that story several times in the Carlton building. As soon as we heard his opening remarks, we knew that once his talk box was opened, there would be no stopping. The lights in the theater had already dimmed, and Huaiqiu took the opportunity to say, "Oh dear, I don't have time to put on makeup!"

Leisurely Painting the Entertainment World (21) Yunnan Opera

— Written by Dongyun, Illustrated by Xiuyan

Yunnan Opera is a unique local opera in Yunnan and is similar to Peking Opera in appearance.

Various local operas can be seen in Shanghai; only Yunnan Opera has not yet had a "chance to meet" the people of Shanghai.

The scripts, scenes, and performances are all the same as Peking Opera, only the pronunciation, dialogue, and clown's interludes maintain the "Yunnan scenery."

In addition, the use of a tanggu drum for rhythm in each play is also unique to Yunnan Opera.

Anecdotes from the Pear Garden

— Xu Muyun

Old Actors Rely on Skill to Make a Living, New Performers Rely on Building the Crowd to Make Money

The first day's opening play, "Wang Baochuan," sold out completely. The grand scenes of the second and third days were not much diminished. The people who came to listen to the opera, because they saw in the golden advertisement the news that Wang Yaoqing, the old court musician, was "personally supervising the scene," so all those who sat in the lower arena (connoisseurs who watched the opera liked to find seats in front of the lower arena door) invariably craned their necks before Yurong was about to appear on stage, looking straight into the upper arena door. Sure enough, they saw an old man wearing dark glasses, extending two fingers towards the musicians and drummers on stage, using hand signals to make a greeting. Thus, Yurong stepped onto the stage amid thunderous applause. According to the rules of opera performance in the past, there was no such thing as a private huqin. Famous actors among the court musicians, such as Gui Fen, Tan Xinpei, and Sun Juxian, etc., such famous figures, never used exclusive musicians and drummers. Among those famous actors, there were only Mei Yutian and Sun Zuochen who played the huqin. As for when each person was about to go on stage, they always extended two or three fingers towards the stage, which was an indication to the person playing the instrument to use the flute to tune the strings to the correct palace tune or B character tune. Only Gui Fen's voice was the best, and the tune was particularly high. Every time he appeared on stage, he simply flicked his sleeves, implying that no matter what three limits you set, I don't care if you want me to sing the upper word tune. However, at that time, it was very common to be able to sing the B character tune. Like Old Tan, who could only eat the tune to the correct palace, he was still ridiculed at the time as being softly decadent. As for those who sang the six-character tune, they simply had no qualifications to perform on stage. (143)
